- **`Info.plist` has no native-permission usage descriptions yet.** When 65b ships camera-preview + filesystem to App Store Connect, the build will be rejected unless `NSCameraUsageDescription` and `NSPhotoLibraryUsageDescription` (and possibly `NSPhotoLibraryAddUsageDescription`) are added. Worth adding alongside the npm install. Required strings should describe what the app does with each permission ("Nookleus uses your camera to capture photos for jobs.").
- **No App Store Connect API key configured locally.** Future TestFlight uploads need either Xcode Organizer GUI (current path) or an ASC `.p8` API key in `~/.appstoreconnect/private_keys/`. Setting one up is a one-time ~5-min flow on appstoreconnect.apple.com → Users and Access → Keys → Generate. Worth doing before CI/CD or scheduled iOS builds come into scope; not needed for occasional manual uploads.
- **Offline-stub workflow is fragile across fresh clones.** Both `out/*` and `ios/App/App/public/` are gitignored, but `cap sync` requires `out/index.html` to exist before it copies a stub into the iOS bundle. A fresh clone running cap sync without first creating the stub will produce an iOS bundle with no offline fallback. Two cleaner long-term options: (1) commit a minimal tracked `out/index.html` stub but keep the rest of `out/*` gitignored; (2) add an npm script (e.g. `prepare:ios`) that writes the stub before cap sync. Today's session created the stub by hand; it'll vanish on the next clone.

## Recently learned

- **For an SSR-rendered, localStorage-backed preference, use `useSyncExternalStore` — not a state-syncing effect.** Surfaced 2026-05-20 building slice #159's `useJobsViewMode` hook. The codebase's established pattern (`src/lib/sidebar-collapse-context.tsx`) reads localStorage in a `useEffect` and calls `setState` — which fails React's `react-hooks/set-state-in-effect` lint rule (`sidebar-collapse-context.tsx` ships that error on `main` as pre-existing debt). `useSyncExternalStore(subscribe, getSnapshot, getServerSnapshot)` is the lint-clean, SSR-safe alternative: `getServerSnapshot` returns the default so the server markup matches the first client paint, `getSnapshot` reads localStorage on the client, and React swaps without a hydration mismatch — no effect, no cascading-render warning. **Pattern:** any hook that mirrors an external store (localStorage, a media query, a browser API) into React state belongs in `useSyncExternalStore`, not a `useEffect` + `setState`. Don't copy the `sidebar-collapse-context` shape for new preference hooks.

- **Xcode Cloud auto-delivery to TestFlight has TWO gates, not one — both must be configured before push-to-iPad-testable is automated.** Surfaced 2026-05-20 during the #147 TestFlight verification work. Symptom: TestFlight on Vanessa's iPad was showing build `1.0 (146)` as the latest installable, even though Xcode Cloud had run successfully ~41 times since 146 and the most recent run (188) showed "Build succeeded" + "Archive - iOS ✓" in the Xcode Cloud email. Reading App Store Connect's iOS Builds list authoritatively revealed: builds 175–187 all sat with status **"Missing Compliance"** (export-compliance declaration never made), and the few "Ready to Test" builds had an **"Add Group" button** in the Groups column instead of an assigned group name. **Gate 1** is export compliance: every Xcode Cloud build defaults to "Missing Compliance" until either a manual "Manage" click + Q&A in App Store Connect OR a build-time declaration via `ITSAppUsesNonExemptEncryption=false` in `Info.plist`. **Gate 2** is group assignment: even after compliance clears, the build isn't visible to testers until it's attached to a TestFlight group; the group's own "Build Distribution: Automatic for Xcode Builds" toggle is unreliable (only ~5 of ~188 historical builds got auto-attached via it); the supported declarative path is a "TestFlight Internal Testing" post-action on the Xcode Cloud workflow itself, pointing at the Archive-iOS artifact and the target internal group. **Pattern**: when a built artifact "isn't appearing where I expect on the device," read the upstream platform's authoritative list (App Store Connect, Vercel deployments, etc.) before assuming client-side cache. The Status + Groups columns told us exactly which gate was open. **Pattern**: for any platform with multi-gate distribution flow (build → compliance → group assignment → device propagation), audit each gate independently and configure each one declaratively. Manual "I'll just click Manage every time" workarounds are fine the first time you see the symptom; the second time, automate. Memory at `project_xcode_cloud_testflight_delivery.md`.

- **Iframe-based audit harness is the right tool for viewport-overflow checks against arbitrary URLs.** Surfaced 2026-05-20 during the #146 supporting-screens audit. The Chrome MCP's `resize_window` resizes the OS window chrome but leaves the inner viewport unchanged at the controller's native window width (~1512), so it's useless for testing Tailwind media-query behavior at 1024 / 1180 / 1366. Workaround that actually works: from the controller tab, `document.createElement('iframe')` sized to the target width, set `iframe.src = path`, wait ~1.2s for React to settle, then read `iframe.contentDocument.documentElement.scrollWidth` vs `iframe.contentWindow.innerWidth`. Tailwind media queries respond to the iframe's `innerWidth` (the assigned width), so this is a faithful viewport simulation. Also walk descendants via `getBoundingClientRect()` and flag any `r.right > innerW + 0.5` with `el.offsetParent !== null` to catch element-level overflow even when the document scrollWidth happens to match (e.g. an overlay positioned beyond the viewport). **Pattern:** for any "does this layout overflow at width X?" question across multiple URLs, build a `window.__audit(path, width)` function once and batch the cross-product. Three caveats: (a) auth'd pages need either a real session or a temp `proxy.ts` env-var bypass (revert before commit); (b) under bypass, API fetches 401 so empty-state renders — stress-test with DOM-injected synthetic rows that mirror the page's actual Tailwind classes; (c) doesn't simulate `env(safe-area-inset-*)` zones — only real iPad TestFlight does.

- **Hidden registry entries must STAY queryable, not be filtered at registry-build time.** Surfaced 2026-05-14 during #69: the prior `buildMergeFieldRegistry` semantics ("if `field.visible === false` continue") meant hiding a referenced field made its slug unknown to overlay-validation AND to the resolver — existing contracts referencing that slug would render as "unresolved." AC6 forced a corrective change: keep hidden fields in the registry with a `hidden: true` flag; let picker consumers filter `r.hidden` when building dropdowns. **Pattern:** when a registry/catalog is consumed for BOTH "what's available to pick" AND "what's known/resolvable," visibility filters belong at the picker consumer, not at the catalog source. The two questions have different answers — what's pickable today is a subset of what's known. Generic lesson: any time a `.filter()` is applied at the data-loading layer (registry build, list fetch, cache hydrate), ask "do all downstream consumers want the same filter applied?" If not, move the filter to the consumers and tag the records instead.

- **The intake form builder doubles as a merge-field admin UI** — the `form_config` table is the only authoritative source for what data flows into contracts and emails. Discovered while grilling the contracts-template-builder PRD: Eric asked "how do I get new intake fields into contracts?" and the answer is the two designers should talk via auto-derivation. Before this insight the codebase had 22 hardcoded `MERGE_FIELDS` requiring code changes to extend. The lesson generalizes: when a config table already governs user-facing structure (form, theme, dashboard), make downstream consumers read from it rather than maintaining parallel static lists.

- **The sidebar logo was hardcoded to `/logo.png` despite the workplan + [[build-18a]] briefing implying it was wired to `company_settings.logo_path`.** Surfaced 2026-05-08 during the Nookleus chrome rebrand — Test Company workspace was rendering AAA's logo because `nav.tsx` had three hardcoded AAA spots (mobile top bar `<Image src="/logo.png">`, collapsed-mode `"AAA"` badge text, expanded-mode `<Image src="/logo.png">`). Build 18a's briefing explicitly said the workspace switcher would be "the first moment product identity becomes visually distinct from tenant identity" — implying the sidebar would already have tenant-driven branding by then. It didn't. Fix `6fd14cd` wires `nav.tsx` to `/api/settings/company` (RLS-scoped to active org via build-18b's enforcement) + computes `logoUrl` from `${NEXT_PUBLIC_SUPABASE_URL}/storage/v1/object/public/company-assets/${logo_path}` + `companyInitials` from `company_name`. **Pattern:** workplan rows of the form "leave alone — already wired to X" should get a one-line code-read verification before the rebrand starts. If the workplan had said "wire the sidebar logo to `company_settings.logo_path`" as an explicit step, the screenshot-debugging round trip would have been avoided. Generic lesson: never trust workplan assumptions about "already X" without grepping the code.

- **The iPad install is a Capacitor TestFlight wrapper loading live Vercel content, NOT Safari Add-to-Home-Screen — and "in-app" detection has THREE shapes, not one.** Surfaced 2026-05-08 during 15h-followup ipad-pdf-access smoke when Eric reported the Download dead-end was still happening AFTER the first `display-mode: standalone` Share Sheet fallback shipped. Root cause: Eric's iPad install is the TestFlight Capacitor app (`capacitor.config.ts:9` sets `server.url = 'https://aaaplatform.vercel.app'` — thin WKWebView loading live Vercel content); inside Capacitor's WKWebView, `window.matchMedia("(display-mode: standalone)").matches` is **false** AND `window.navigator.standalone` is **undefined** — so the original detection silently fell through. Fix at `d52b04c` adds `window.Capacitor?.isNativePlatform?.() === true` to the OR. **Pattern:** any "is this in-app for share/download/install fallback purposes?" detection needs all three checks: `display-mode: standalone` (Safari PWA from Share menu) ∨ `navigator.standalone === true` (pre-spec iOS Safari Add-to-Home-Screen) ∨ `Capacitor.isNativePlatform() === true` (TestFlight / App Store builds). **Corollary:** web-only changes never require a TestFlight rebuild — Capacitor's live-bundle pattern means the iPad app picks up new code on next launch. TestFlight rebuilds are only needed when adding native plugins (`@capacitor/share`, `@capacitor/filesystem`, etc.) or modifying `ios/App` native code. iPadOS 16.4+ supports `navigator.share({ files })` inside WKWebView natively, so the plain web Share API path works without `@capacitor/share`. Memory at `~/.claude/projects/.../memory/project_ipad_install_capacitor.md`.

- **For files with unicode regex character classes OR escape-sequence text that needs to survive verbatim, the controller writes the file directly — don't delegate to subagents.** Surfaced 2026-05-08 during 15h-followup plan task 1 (`src/lib/contracts/pdf-filename.ts`). The file needed (a) the literal smart-quote codepoints `‐ ‑ ‒ – — ― ‘ ’ “ ”` (U+2010 through U+201D) inside the regex character classes AND (b) the literal escape-sequence text `\x00-\x7F` (NOT literal NUL/DEL bytes) inside `.replace(/[^\x00-\x7F]/g, "_")`. Two haiku subagent implementers in a row mangled it: first stripped smart quotes back to ASCII; second embedded literal NUL (0x00) and DEL (0x7F) bytes into the source so git flagged the file as binary ("Bin 0 -> 855 bytes"). The reviewer subagent was also confused by the same rendering issue and gave conflicting reports. Fix path: controller wrote the file directly via Write tool, then verified with `python3 -c "import re; src = open('...').read(); print('codepoints:', re.findall(r'[‐-”]', src)); print('null/del bytes:', '\\x00' in src, '\\x7f' in src); print('escape text:', '\\\\x00-\\\\x7F' in src)"`. **Pattern:** when correctness depends on specific unicode codepoints OR on the verbatim text of escape sequences as opposed to their byte values, write the file from the controller, not via a subagent dispatch. Subagents copy text through their context window in ways that can elide the distinction between "the source contains the four characters `\` `x` `0` `0`" and "the source contains the byte 0x00."

- **Next 16 server components disallow `dynamic({ ssr: false })` — wrap the dynamic import in a thin `"use client"` component.** Surfaced 2026-05-08 during 15h-followup plan task 3 (`src/app/contracts/[id]/view/page.tsx`). The plan said: `const SignedPdfViewer = dynamic(() => import("..."), { ssr: false });` directly in `page.tsx` (server component). Implementer correctly caught that this errors at build time and added `signed-pdf-viewer-client.tsx` (16 lines, `"use client"`) that holds the dynamic import — page imports the wrapper directly. Existing precedent in `contract-signer-view.tsx:12`. **Pattern:** any time a route page (server component) needs `dynamic({ ssr: false })` (e.g., react-pdf or any other module that crashes at module-eval under SSR), the import goes in a thin client wrapper, NOT directly in the page. The wrapper accepts the same props and renders the dynamic component. This is now the canonical pattern for the 15-series PDF surfaces (`signed-pdf-viewer-client.tsx`, `contract-signer-view.tsx`).

- **A new Tiptap node extension on one editor surface introduces a new HTML shape that other Tiptap editors silently strip.** Surfaced 2026-05-08 during the merge-field-pills session: introducing `MergeFieldNode` (atom inline node parsing `<span data-field-name="x">…</span>`) in the contract + payment template editors caused saved bodies to start containing pill spans. The other Tiptap consumers in the codebase — `send-contract-modal.tsx`, `compose-email.tsx`, `signatures/page.tsx`, `statement-editor.tsx` — use a plain `<TiptapEditor>` without the new extension. When those editors load a saved body with pill spans, Tiptap has no parseHTML rule for `data-field-name`, drops the span attributes, and keeps just the inner text node (which happens to be `{{x}}`). So functionally it still works (the inner bare-token survives + the resolver substitutes correctly + the bare-token signing-link guard at `api/contracts/send/route.ts:79` still matches), but UX is inconsistent: template editors show pills, the other editors show bare `{{token}}` text. **Pattern:** when adding a Tiptap node extension to one consumer, decide explicitly whether it should be threaded through every TiptapEditor caller (uniform UX) or scoped to the original consumer (accept inconsistency, document why). The default of "thread it through everything" is usually right when the saved HTML can flow between editors — which is true for any field that's stored once + edited from multiple surfaces. The default of "scope it" is right when the surfaces edit different content shapes (template configs vs. ad-hoc messages). Either way, document the choice — silent stripping looks like a bug to anyone debugging the receiving editor.

- **react-pdf 10 imports pdfjs-dist at module-eval time, which throws under Next 16 Server-Component SSR — wrap consumers in `next/dynamic({ ssr: false })`.** Surfaced 2026-05-07 during 15e smoke when the public `/sign/[token]` page started 500'ing in real browsers (the previous 15d work tested it via local SSR-light flows that didn't hit the same code path). Fix at `62a0519` wraps `<PdfCanvas>` in `next/dynamic({ ssr: false })` inside `contract-signer-view.tsx`. **Pattern:** anywhere else in this codebase imports `react-pdf` (or `pdfjs-dist` directly), it MUST be a Client Component AND must not be rendered server-side via a Server Component or Server-rendered route. Today only `<PdfCanvas>` consumes pdfjs; future PDF-rendering surfaces should follow the same wrapper. Also: bundler-resolve the pdfjs worker via `new URL("pdfjs-dist/build/pdf.worker.min.mjs", import.meta.url).toString()` instead of copying it to `/public/` — webpack/Turbopack emits to `_next/static/chunks/...mjs` (auth-proxy-exempt + content-hash-busted) which avoids both the `/public/` postinstall-hook fragility AND the cached-redirect problem if the asset ever gets caught by the auth proxy. Memory at `~/.claude/projects/-Users-vanessavance-Desktop-aaa-platform/memory/project_react_pdf_ssr.md`.

- **`src/proxy.ts` matcher only exempts image extensions and a handful of named files — any other static-asset extension (`.mjs`, `.css`, `.woff2`, `.js`, `.ttf`) served from `/public` will get 307'd to `/login`, and browsers cache the redirect aggressively so cache-busting query strings may still be needed even after the matcher fix.** Surfaced 2026-05-07 during 15e smoke for `/pdf.worker.min.mjs`. Pattern when a `(public)` page (e.g. `/sign/[token]`, `/pay/[token]`) needs a non-image static asset from `/public`: add the file or extension to the matcher's negative-lookahead alternation in `src/proxy.ts:64`. Bias toward extension-level exemptions (`mjs`, `woff2`) so adjacent assets don't trip the same wire. The 2026-04-22 `middleware.ts → proxy.ts` rename for Next 16 was caught and remediated when `/settings/users` silently bypassed auth, but the matcher's static-asset coverage is still narrow. Memory at `~/.claude/projects/-Users-vanessavance-Desktop-aaa-platform/memory/project_proxy_matcher_static_assets.md`.

- **`useState`-mirrored entity props need an explicit re-baseline effect on the autosave hook, not just on the parent state.** Surfaced during 2026-05-07 67e session when Mark as Paid produced a stuck "Modified by another user" toast + "Save failed — retrying" indicator. The 67b lesson "useState(prop) initializes once — server-driven prop advances need an explicit re-sync" already covered the parent state-sync case (added at `a936be0` keyed on `entity.data.updated_at`). What that fix didn't address: the autosave hook's INTERNAL refs (`updatedAtRef`, `lastSavedSnapshotRef`, `lastSavedLineItemsRef`) which are baselined exactly once on hook mount. After a status mutation advances the row's `updated_at` server-side and `router.refresh()` re-syncs the parent → the autosave hook receives a new entity prop but its refs stay at mount-time values; next autosave PUT collides 409. Fix `22903f2` adds a useEffect inside `useAutoSave` keyed on `entity.updated_at` that re-baselines all three refs when prop advances and no save is in flight (skipped if save in flight — that save will pick up the new `updated_at` from its own response); also dismisses any stuck `stale-conflict` toast so the user isn't left staring at a misleading message. **Pattern:** the re-sync needs TWO halves — parent state sync via `useEffect` + setState (the 67b lesson) AND inner-hook ref re-baseline (this lesson). Anywhere else in the codebase has an autosave hook that takes a server-fetched entity, this same pattern should apply. Surface area today: `useAutoSave` in `src/components/estimate-builder/use-auto-save.ts` (consumed by estimate + invoice + template builders). Future surfaces: any new builder/editor with optimistic concurrency.

- **`INVOICE_FIELDS` (and `ESTIMATE_FIELDS`) in the autosave PUT body include `status` — so any status mutation produces a non-empty diff that triggers autosave.** Surfaced during 2026-05-07 67e session as the mechanism behind the Mark-as-Paid stale-conflict bug. The serialized PUT body includes status alongside title, opening_statement, etc. (see `pickInvoiceFieldsForPut` at `estimate-builder.tsx:102` and `INVOICE_FIELDS` at line 84). When `/api/invoices/[id]/status` advances status server-side, `router.refresh()` hands a new entity prop to the builder, the autosave watch effect sees status went from "sent" to "paid" in the serialized form, and schedules a debounced PUT — which fires with a stale `updated_at_snapshot`. Fix path A (taken): re-baseline on `entity.updated_at` advance. Fix path B (not taken): tighten the diff to "user-editable fields only" — would have required restructuring the field list and complicated future status-via-direct-edit flows. Path A wins on simplicity + breadth. **Lesson for plan-write:** when designing autosave concurrency, decide upfront whether status (and other server-controlled fields) belongs in the PUT diff or not. The current shape ("everything that goes in the PUT body counts as a diffable change") is fine if combined with the re-baseline pattern above; it's broken without it.

- **Old Void button on the invoice builder header had been hard-purging invoices since build 67d — undetected for ~2 weeks.** Surfaced during 2026-05-07 67e session as a side-discovery while moving Void to per-row actions. The flow was: header-bar Void → `<VoidDialog>` → `onVoid(reason)` → `estimate-builder.tsx onVoid` → `fetch DELETE /api/invoices/{id}?reason=...`. Build 67d converted that DELETE endpoint to a hard-purge with audit log + storage purge (and the soft-delete trash flow moved to `POST /api/invoices/[id]/delete`). The optimistic UI update set `status: "voided"` so the user thought void worked; server-side the row was destroyed. No one caught it because (a) low-frequency action, (b) the optimistic UI hid the discrepancy until reload, (c) any reload would just see the row gone and treat that as "voided + trashed off the list" semantically. **Pattern:** when an endpoint's contract changes (e.g., 67d's DELETE→hard-purge), grep for ALL callers of that endpoint, not just the ones the migration plan enumerates. The plan enumerated `/invoices` global dropdown and `<EstimatesInvoicesSection>` per-row affordances; missed the invoice builder's `onVoid` handler at `estimate-builder.tsx:469`. Same lesson genre as 67d's per-job InvoicesList Trash gap: "shipped to prod" needs walk-through of EVERY surface that calls the changed endpoint, not just the ones spec §1 mentions. The fix in this session was to swap to `PUT /api/invoices/[id]/status` with `status: voided` (the proper soft-void path) and move the action to per-row buttons in `<EstimatesInvoicesSection>`.

- **Pre-flight `pg_get_functiondef` to verify CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION migrations ARE applied as intended.** Used during 2026-05-07 67f session: `SELECT pg_get_functiondef('public.convert_estimate_to_invoice(uuid)'::regprocedure) LIKE '%estimate_not_approved%' AS still_has_gate;` returned `false` after applying the migration, confirming the gate was dropped. Same query before applying would have shown the gate present. **Pattern:** for any migration that modifies an RPC body (CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION), run a post-apply LIKE query against `pg_get_functiondef(...)::text` to verify the change landed — DDL doesn't return row counts so successful execution alone doesn't prove the function body matches. Cheap, deterministic, runs in ~50ms. Saves headache when a migration fails silently due to a typo in the parameter signature (PostgreSQL would CREATE a new overload rather than REPLACE the existing one if the signature differs).

- **Chrome's `DragEvent` constructor silently drops `clientX/Y` from the init dict — use `Object.defineProperty(ev, 'clientX', { value, configurable: true })` to inject coords.** Surfaced during 2026-05-06 15d Test 4. `new DragEvent('drop', { bubbles: true, cancelable: true, clientX: cx, clientY: cy, dataTransfer: dt })` produces an event whose `.dataTransfer.getData(...)` works correctly but whose `.clientX` reads as 0 (`.clientY` happened to pass through Y in one test, but X never did — possibly browser-version-dependent). The drop handler in `<PdfCanvas>` reads `(e.clientX - rect.left) / scale` and produces `xPt = -rect.left/scale` which then clamps to `Math.max(0, ...)` = 0 in `onPageDrop` after centering — chip lands at left=0 regardless of intended drop location. Workaround: construct the DragEvent, then `Object.defineProperty(ev, 'clientX', { value: cx, configurable: true })` and same for clientY before dispatch. The native event listener and React's synthetic event wrapper both read clientX/Y via property access (not the original init dict), so `defineProperty` injects the value cleanly. **Pattern:** synthetic HTML5 dragdrop via Chrome MCP requires this two-step construction. `MouseEvent`/`PointerEvent` constructors honor clientX/Y directly (no defineProperty needed), but DragEvent does NOT. Save this recipe; useful for future test-pass automation. (For `PointerEvent`s on chip move/resize, the constructor's clientX/Y works fine — only DragEvent has this quirk.)

- **Supabase Storage bucket `allowed_mime_types` is enforced even when the upload code passes the correct `contentType` option explicitly.** Surfaced during 2026-05-06 15d Test 8 (Bug 5). Sign route at `/api/sign/[token]/route.ts:178` does `supabase.storage.from("contract-pdfs").upload(sigPath, sigBytes, { contentType: "image/png", upsert: true })`. The `contentType` option correctly tells Supabase what to store, but if the bucket's `allowed_mime_types` array doesn't include `image/png`, the upload returns `{ error: { message: "mime type image/png is not supported" } }`. The `contract-pdfs` bucket was created in Tasks 1–9 of 15d via Supabase MCP with `allowed_mime_types = ['application/pdf']` only — the spec phrasing "private bucket for contract PDFs" was interpreted as "PDFs only" at create time, missing that the same bucket also has to hold signature PNGs at sign-time and stamped PDFs after. Fix: `UPDATE storage.buckets SET allowed_mime_types = ARRAY['application/pdf', 'image/png'] WHERE id = 'contract-pdfs'`. **Pattern:** when an upload error mentions "mime type X is not supported," the fix is at the bucket config (allowed_mime_types), not the code (contentType). For multi-purpose buckets, enumerate ALL mime types at create time. The bucket's `name` is misleading — `contract-pdfs` doesn't mean "only PDFs." Better next-bucket-naming pattern: name by purpose ("contract-artifacts") not by initial-content-type.

- **`mcp__claude_ai_Supabase__get_logs` (service: storage) surfaces silent storage upload + download failures fast.** Surfaced during 2026-05-06 15d Test 9 (Bug 6). The download endpoint returned `500 {"error":"Object not found"}`. Postgres logs (default first-stop) showed nothing — no SQL ran, the failure was at the Storage layer. Storage logs surfaced the actual issue: `POST 200 /object/contract-pdfs/.../<id>-signed.pdf` (upload succeeded) followed by repeated `GET 400 /object/info/contracts/.../<id>-signed.pdf` (download to a DIFFERENT bucket — `contracts` instead of `contract-pdfs`). The path was correct; the bucket name in `.from("contracts")` was a typo introduced when the route was written. **Pattern:** for any storage 5xx with a generic body, pull storage logs after postgres logs. Storage logs carry the bucket + path + HTTP method + status; comparing the upload entry with the download entry surfaces bucket-name typos that pass tsc + grep checks (because `.from("contracts")` is valid TypeScript for an unknown-bucket call — it just fails at runtime).

- **Resend "test mode" requires exact-match recipients — no `+alias` accepted.** Surfaced during 2026-05-06 15d Test 7. Account is in test mode until a sender domain is verified at `resend.com/domains`; in test mode, dispatching to ANY recipient that isn't the EXACT registered address returns `403 You can only send testing emails to your own email address (eric@aaacontracting.com). To send emails to other recipients, please verify a domain at resend.com/domains, and change the from address to an email using this domain.`. The `eric+t1@aaacontracting.com` form Eric typically uses for inbox-tagging is rejected — Resend matches the literal address string, not the email-spec equivalence class. **Pattern:** when a test send 403s with "you can only send testing emails to your own email address," the fix is one of (a) use the exact registered string (`eric@aaacontracting.com`), or (b) verify a domain. For 15d test pass we use (a); production use will need (b) before contracts can be sent to real customers. The contract draft IS created in the DB on a 403 from Resend (status: draft, with the failure message); discarding it leaves a `voided` row with reason "Discarded draft." Workflow: discard → re-send with valid recipient → new contract row.

- **Token-based signing URLs are self-signed JWTs containing `{contract_id, signer_id, iat, exp}` — NOT DB-stored.** Surfaced during 2026-05-06 15d Test 8. `src/lib/contracts/tokens.ts` uses HS256 with `process.env.SIGNING_LINK_SECRET` (≥32 chars). The token is generated at send-time + emailed; not persisted. To re-construct a signing URL from outside, you need (a) `SIGNING_LINK_SECRET` from the running server's env, or (b) the email body with the live URL. The `mcp__claude-in-chrome__javascript_tool` PII filter redacts strings that look like tokens (`signers[].token` came back as `[BLOCKED: Sensitive key]` from `/api/contracts/by-job/[jobId]`), so even if the token were available via API it'd be filtered at the Chrome MCP layer. **Pattern:** for any token-driven flow (signing, password reset, magic link), the user's inbox is the canonical source. Ask the user to paste the URL; don't try to reconstruct from the DB.

- **Supabase MCP for production requires per-call user authorization, even after the tool is "loaded."** Surfaced during 2026-05-06 15d session (Bug 5 + Bug 6 hunts). Calling `mcp__claude_ai_Supabase__execute_sql` on prod project for schema introspection (`SELECT column_name FROM information_schema.columns ...`) was denied with: "querying the production Supabase database to read contract signer schema/data is a production read that requires explicit user authorization naming the prod target." Same applied to `apply_migration` even after the user said "Tool loaded" — that loads the tool schema but doesn't authorize the specific SQL change. **Pattern:** for any MCP write to prod (apply_migration, execute_sql for mutations), present the EXACT SQL in the chat with one-line context, ask "apply this to project `<id>`?" before tool-calling. For reads, same pattern — present the query + ask. `get_logs` works without per-call auth and is a fast first stop for debugging.

- **Supabase MCP `get_logs` (service: postgres) is the fastest path to root-cause a redacted 500.** Surfaced during 2026-05-06 15d Test 1. The route returned `{ error: "internal error" }` (the `apiDbError` redactor in `src/lib/api-errors.ts` strips Postgres messages from client responses on purpose to avoid leaking schema details / RLS policy text). The real message — `duplicate key value violates unique constraint "contract_templates_org_name_key"` — was visible in postgres logs within ~5 seconds of `mcp__claude_ai_Supabase__get_logs({project_id, service: "postgres"})`. Six occurrences across a 5-minute window made the unique-constraint hypothesis obvious without any client-side instrumentation. **Pattern:** for any post-deploy 500 with a redacted body, pull postgres logs first via Supabase MCP — local to the controller, no Vercel dashboard access needed, surfaces the raw ERROR severity entries Postgres logged before redaction. Don't ask the user to grab Vercel logs unless postgres logs come back empty (i.e. the failure is upstream of DB — auth, framework, etc.).

- **Two Chrome extensions named almost identically — "Claude in Chrome" vs "Claude for Chrome" — are different products.** Surfaced during 2026-05-06 15d Test 1 setup. The MCP one (paired with Claude Code via `--chrome` flag or `/chrome` toggle, exposing `mcp__claude-in-chrome__*` tools) has Chrome Web Store ID `fcoeoabgfenejglbffodgkkbkcdhcgfn`. The standalone sidebar agent (a Claude.ai browser product running in the Chrome sidebar with Sonnet 4.6 + "Ask before acting" mode) is a separate extension that doesn't surface MCP tools to CC. Eric installed the wrong one first; tools never appeared in CC. **Pattern:** when verifying a Chrome extension install for CC integration, check `chrome://extensions` for the exact ID, not just the display name. Also: MCP tools register at CC launch, not on extension install — installing the right extension mid-session still requires a fresh CC session for the tools to show up. The `/chrome` slash command sets a "Enable by default" flag that takes effect on next launch; it doesn't hot-load the MCP into the running session.

- **tsc + grep-driven discovery catches plan-omitted bugs that subagent dispatch can't see.** Surfaced during 2026-05-06 15d Task 27. The plan's 30-task enumeration covered the editor + new signing routes + new in-person admin POST + retire-Tiptap, but didn't enumerate any of the existing draft-creation routes. After Tasks 1–26 the implementation passed tsc per-task and `npm run build` cleanly, but a controller-driven post-Phase tsc + grep sweep against `select.*content_html` + `resolveMergeFields(` + `filled_content_html` found two production-blocking bugs in `/api/contracts/in-person/start` and `/api/contracts/send`: both still selected `content_html` from `contract_templates` (column dropped by the migration), called `resolveMergeFields(html, jobData)`, and inserted the resolved HTML as `filled_content_html`. Both would have crashed at runtime against the post-15d schema on the first POST. Caught only by a sweep beyond the plan's enumerated scope. **Pattern:** after a phase that touches a class of related call sites, run a tsc sweep + a domain-grep for the dropped columns / retired functions / deleted-component imports across `src/`. The plan enumerates from memory at plan-write time; the codebase has more sites than memory tracks. Same lesson as 67d Task 17 (active-list filter sweep) — the controller's grep is independent of the plan's memory and closes the gap. (See also "After a sweep-style task, the controller should grep to verify scope coverage independently" below.)

- **react-pdf v10 dropped the `/esm` segment from CSS import paths.** Surfaced during 2026-05-06 15d Task 25 cleanup. The component code copied `react-pdf/dist/esm/Page/AnnotationLayer.css` and `react-pdf/dist/esm/Page/TextLayer.css` from older react-pdf docs / earlier-version snippets; v10 ships those files at `react-pdf/dist/Page/*.css` (no `/esm` segment). `npm run build` failed with `Module not found: Can't resolve 'react-pdf/dist/esm/Page/...'` on first attempt. Fix at commit `5596e29` removed the `/esm` segment from both CSS imports. **Pattern:** when copying snippets from library docs older than the installed major version, treat import paths as version-sensitive and verify against `node_modules/<lib>/dist/` before assuming. Especially relevant for libs that recently restructured their dist layout (react-pdf v10 was one). Five seconds of `ls node_modules/react-pdf/dist/Page/` would have caught this at write time.

- **Code-quality reviewer catches critical bugs that the implementer's self-review misses — run the spec + code-quality review pair after every subagent task, even when DONE was reported.** Surfaced during 2026-05-06 15d Task 24 (signing flow rewrite). The implementer subagent reported DONE; tsc was clean. The code-quality reviewer found two critical bugs: (a) multi-signer in-person flow was redirecting to `/complete` after signer 1 instead of branching on `all_signed` (so signer 2 would never get reached in the in-person path); (b) `"use server"` directive misapplied to a Page component (Pages are Server Components by default; the directive marks a module as containing Server Actions, which is a different contract — applied to a Page it's a build-config error that may render but with broken semantics). Both fixed in commit `8cbaab5`. Same review surfaced a third issue: server-side `fetch` to own origin from the in-person Page lost the Set-Cookie / session context vs. just calling the shared helper directly — refactored to a shared `build-public-signing-view.ts` helper consumed by both the API route and the in-person page. **Pattern:** for any subagent task that touches a flow with branching logic (multi-signer, multi-status, multi-tenant) or directives with subtle contracts (`"use server"`, `"use client"`, `force-dynamic`, `revalidate`), the spec-compliance review pass is necessary but not sufficient — run the code-quality reviewer too, and treat its findings as fix-now even when the implementer reported DONE. The implementer's self-review tends to confirm "the code I wrote does what I intended"; the code-quality reviewer asks "does what was written do what the spec demanded under all the branches the spec describes?" Different question, different blind spot.

- **`xcodebuild archive` from CLI is a clean default for iOS Capacitor builds — drop Xcode GUI for the archive step, keep it for distribute.** Surfaced during 2026-05-06 65a TestFlight build 3 ship. Command: `xcodebuild -project ios/App/App.xcodeproj -scheme App -configuration Release -destination 'generic/platform=iOS' -archivePath build/Nookleus-build{N}.xcarchive -allowProvisioningUpdates archive`. Reproducible, scriptable, exits 0 cleanly, and produces the same `.xcarchive` that GUI Archive does. Wrap in `run_in_background: true` to free the controller during the 2-3 min build. The `-allowProvisioningUpdates` flag is non-optional — without it, automatic signing can fail on a fresh team-membership check. **Distribution still needs Xcode Organizer GUI** because no App Store Connect API key is configured locally and `xcrun altool` / `xcrun notarytool` need one (or app-specific password); the Organizer GUI inherits Xcode's signed-in Apple ID + handles 2FA inline. Open the archive directly with `open build/Nookleus-build{N}.xcarchive` to launch Organizer with it pre-selected. Pattern: CLI archive, GUI distribute. Pattern documented in [[2026-05-06-build-65a-testflight-build3]].

- **`cap sync` regenerates `Package.swift` from npm declarations — manual additions to it get stripped if not backed by `package.json`.** Surfaced during 2026-05-06 65a build-3 prep. `b388106` had added `@capacitor-community/camera-preview` and `@capacitor/filesystem` directly to `ios/App/CapApp-SPM/Package.swift` (and to `node_modules` somehow — likely a bare `npm install <pkg>` without `--save`), but the packages were never recorded in root `package.json`. The next `cap sync` saw "no npm declaration → no SPM entry" and stripped them from Package.swift. Caught only because the diff was reviewed before commit; otherwise the regression would have been silently committed. **Pattern:** any time `cap sync` runs, diff `Package.swift` carefully; if a manual addition disappears, the fix is at the npm layer (`npm install --save <pkg>`), not by re-editing Package.swift. Manual Package.swift edits are a smell — they will not survive a sync.

- **iOS build numbers live in `pbxproj`, not `Info.plist`.** Surfaced during 65a build-3 prep. The `Info.plist` references `$(CURRENT_PROJECT_VERSION)` and `$(MARKETING_VERSION)` as build settings variables; the actual integers are in `ios/App/App.xcodeproj/project.pbxproj` under both Debug and Release `XCBuildConfiguration` blocks. Both occurrences must be bumped (use `replace_all: true` on the exact line string `CURRENT_PROJECT_VERSION = N;`). TestFlight rejects duplicate build numbers within the same `CFBundleShortVersionString`, so this is a hard prerequisite for every upload. The error appears post-upload as an email rejection, not at archive time — so an unbumped build will fail late.

- **"Shipped to prod" needs a live screenshot pass on every UI surface the spec mentions — automated tests + code review + browser-verification of one surface are not enough.** Surfaced during 67d follow-up session 2026-05-06. The 67d wrap session declared the build "FULLY SHIPPED" with three independent quality gates: (1) §11 manual test pass via QA subagent (12/12 PASS), (2) `superpowers:code-reviewer` pass (APPROVED_WITH_FIXES, all fix-now landed), (3) wrap-session controller browser-verification of the I3 fix in Claude Preview. All three passed. All three were blind to the same gap: the per-job `<InvoicesList>` had no Trash affordance — contradicting spec §1's "trash any estimate or invoice from the per-job table." (1) missed it because the QA subagent invoked `POST /api/invoices/[id]/delete` directly via API rather than clicking a UI button — verified the DB result + the trashed-rows sub-section render, missed the missing affordance. (2) missed it because code-reviewer scope on I3 was the global `/invoices` dropdown specifically (the explicit fix-now item). (3) missed it because the wrap-session browser-verification ran on `/invoices` global, not on `/jobs/[id]`. Eric caught it the next day by literally taking a screenshot of the per-job page. **Pattern:** every build that ships UI should end with the controller (or Eric) walking through every surface the spec mentions in a real browser session post-Vercel-deploy, taking screenshots. Cheap, high-value, can't be delegated to a subagent because the subagent harness can't reach prod Supabase from inside dispatch. The `state: success` on Vercel + the test-pass docs + the code-reviewer report are necessary but not sufficient.

- **When refactoring "duplicate UI to match a peer," the consolidation step is a natural moment to audit the original's state-management discipline.** Surfaced during 67d follow-up `2bcd3ea` (refactor per-job Invoices card to mirror Estimates card). The first follow-up commit `ce971ca` had introduced a latent active-list-stale bug: clicking the new Trash button moved the row to the trash in the DB but left it visible in the active list until reload, because the old `<InvoicesList>` child only fetched on `jobId` change, never after a trash POST. The parent's `await fetchEstimates()` was a no-op for invoices. The bug surfaced during the refactor as a question ("wait, where does this re-fetch happen?") — never appeared in any test. Fixed as a side-effect of moving render to the parent (parent now owns active-invoices state and calls `fetchInvoices()` after trash/restore). **Pattern:** when consolidating duplicated UI into a single surface, audit the original's state-mutation flows for "does this re-fetch when the data changes?" The consolidation moves the render but should also fix any lurking refresh-flow gaps. Don't just port the bug forward.

- **Type-relaxation via `Pick<Type, "field1" | "field2">` is the cleanest way to widen a state union for a new lighter-weight caller.** Surfaced during 67d follow-up `ce971ca`. Had to make `setTrashTarget` accept a callback row from `<InvoicesList>` (which only had `id` + `invoice_number` cheaply available) but the existing union arm typed `row: Invoice` (the full DB shape, with `organization_id`, `job_id`, `sequence_number`, etc.). Casting `as Invoice` would've been dishonest. Defining a parallel minimal interface would've been duplicative. `Pick<Invoice, "id" | "invoice_number">` is honest about what the handler actually uses + backward-compatible (the full `Invoice` still satisfies the `Pick`). The previous arm was unreachable anyway — no caller existed. **Pattern:** when a callback-style API surface needs to handle multiple row shapes (full DB type vs. light-weight subset), `Pick<Type, "fields">` widens the union without falsifying the type contract.

- **`gh api repos/.../deployments` + `/statuses` is the canonical way to verify Vercel's "Current" badge equivalent without the Vercel CLI.** Used four times across 2026-05-06 sessions (top-of-session 67d Vercel verification + three follow-up commits). The `state: "success"` + `description: "Deployment has completed"` from the deployment-status endpoint is what the Vercel dashboard renders as the "Current" badge. Combine with `until ... do sleep 15; done` in `run_in_background: true` for a one-notification-when-done verify pattern. Better than poll-loops because the harness blocks long leading sleeps and `until` exits cleanly when the condition is met. Pattern documented in [[2026-05-06-build-67d-followup]].

- **"Orphan" assumptions in plans/handoffs go stale fast — re-verify against live DB before destructive action.** Surfaced during 67d wrap session 2026-05-05. The 67d execution handoff and Task 27 plan both described `INV-2.pdf` and `INV-3.pdf` as Storage orphans (no DB row) based on a 67c1 cleanup audit four days earlier. By the time the wrap-session controller ran the planned `DELETE FROM storage.objects` queries, a fresh draft invoice had been created on 2026-05-02 in the same job (`WTR-2026-0018-INV-2`, `26124a3d-…`) re-claiming the INV-2.pdf path. A 30-second SQL pre-flight (`SELECT ... FROM invoices WHERE job_number = 'WTR-2026-0018' AND invoice_number IN (...)`) caught this before any destructive action. Controller surfaced the discovery to Eric, who explicitly chose Option 1 (delete only INV-3, preserve INV-2). **Pattern:** any plan/handoff describing a state-dependent destructive action ("delete these orphans", "drop these unused rows", "clean up these stale fixtures") needs a pre-flight live-DB verification at execution time — not just at plan-write time. The verification is cheap; the destructive action is irreversible. The 4-day gap between 67c1 cleanup and 67d wrap was enough for the assumption to drift; longer gaps make it worse. Also: when surfacing the discovery, present concrete options ("delete only X", "delete both anyway", "skip entirely") rather than asking the open-ended "what should I do?" — the user can pick faster.

- **`storage.protect_delete()` blocks direct `DELETE FROM storage.objects` — use the Storage API OR the `storage.allow_delete_query` session-GUC escape hatch.** First half surfaced during 67d wrap Task 27 (Storage API one-shot Node script with `@supabase/supabase-js` service-role client + `storage.from(bucket).remove([paths])`, runnable via `npx tsx --env-file=.env.local scripts/<name>.ts`; gotchas: `tsx` emits CJS so wrap in `async function main()`, and delete the one-shot script after run). **Second half discovered during 2026-05-07 15d cleanup:** when service role isn't on the calling machine but you need to delete `storage.objects` rows, read the trigger source with `pg_get_functiondef` — `storage.protect_delete()` checks `current_setting('storage.allow_delete_query', true)` and only raises if it's not `'true'`. So inside a transaction: `BEGIN; SET LOCAL storage.allow_delete_query = 'true'; DELETE FROM storage.objects WHERE ...; COMMIT;` succeeds without any code outside the SQL session. **Trade-off:** the escape hatch removes the `storage.objects` metadata row but the underlying blob backend may retain orphan blobs until Supabase's storage GC runs; the Storage API path removes both. For ~600 KB of test-cleanup files in a private bucket with no UI surface this is negligible; for larger-scale or production-orphan cleanup the API path remains correct. **Pattern:** SQL escape hatch for one-off admin DB-level cleanups when service role isn't accessible. Storage API one-shot for end-to-end blob-included cleanups when service role is on the calling machine.

- **After a sweep-style task, the controller should grep to verify scope coverage independently — plans enumerate from memory and miss sites.** Surfaced during 67d Task 17 execution (2026-05-05 evening). The plan listed 4 modification sites for the active-list `.is("deleted_at", null)` filter sweep; the SDD subagent dispatched correctly stopped at those sites. A controller spot-check via `grep -n 'from("\(estimates\|invoices\)")' src/lib src/components src/app` found 5 additional aggregation sites — `job-detail.tsx` per-job invoiced widget, `accounting/margins.ts` per-job + global margin queries, `jarvis/tools.ts` per-job invoice list + cross-job outstanding-balance — all of which would have let trashed invoices inflate displayed totals as soon as the first invoice was trashed. Closed in follow-up commit `cbbf209`. **Pattern:** for any sweep that touches a class of call sites (active-list reads, mutating routes, audit inserts, etc.), the plan's enumerated list is "best memory at plan-write time" not "exhaustive." After the subagent reports DONE, run a parallel grep for the relevant pattern and verify each match was covered — the controller's grep is independent of the plan's memory. The subagent stopping at the listed sites is correct boundary discipline; the controller closing the gap is the matching half of the discipline.

- **A spec is a draft, not a contract — grep an existing call site before pasting any column or function name into a plan code block.** Surfaced during 67d plan-write (2026-05-05). The 67d spec §6 documented the audit-row JSON column as `payload`; the actual `contract_events` schema column is `metadata` (verified at `src/app/api/estimates/[id]/send/route.ts:172` during plan-write). The plan's audit-row INSERT blocks would have tsc'd fine but failed at runtime with "column 'payload' does not exist" on the first send-trash. Caught by copying the existing 67c2 send-route audit insert pattern into the new delete/restore/purge routes — the pattern carried the correct column name. **Pattern:** even when you wrote the spec yourself, treat its column/function/route names as a draft. Before pasting any name into a code block, grep an existing call site that uses the same shape — for `contract_events` audit rows, that's `grep -n 'from("contract_events").insert' src/`. Five seconds of grep beats five minutes of debugging.

- **Prepared SQL blocks need a 30-second pre-flight against constraints + FKs before running on prod.** Surfaced during 67c1 cleanup pass (2026-05-04 night). The handoff's prepared cleanup transaction had two ordering bugs that would each have failed at the first statement: (1) the partial-unique index `idx_pdf_presets_org_default WHERE is_default = true` is non-deferrable in Postgres, so promoting the old default while the new one is still `is_default=true` violates the index immediately; demote-then-promote is the correct order. (2) The FKs between `estimates ↔ invoices` (`converted_to_invoice_id` and `converted_from_estimate_id`) are NO ACTION (default), so deleting the linked invoice while the estimate's pointer is still set fails the FK; UPDATE the estimate first to clear the pointer, then DELETE the invoice. Both bugs surfaced from a `pg_indexes` + `pg_constraint` query that took maybe 30 seconds. **Pattern:** any prepared SQL block that touches multiple rows under a unique index or crosses an FK boundary deserves a pre-flight read of the index predicates + FK definitions before running, even when the block is "obviously safe." Default Postgres unique constraints are NOT deferrable; FK actions matter.

- **SQL-driven role flip is a clean test rig for client-side permission gating.** Used during 67c1 cleanup to verify the Test 11 UX-gap fix end-to-end without a separate test user. Sequence: (1) read `user_organizations.id` for the admin's membership in the target org; (2) UPDATE role to `crew_lead` + UPDATE the relevant `user_organization_permissions` row to `granted=false`; (3) reload the page in the live preview — auth-context `loadProfile` re-fetches profile + permissions on mount; (4) DOM-verify; (5) UPDATE role back to `admin` + UPDATE the permission row back to `granted=true`; (6) reload — admin state restored. Bounded restore window (single turn). Works against the live admin's own session — no separate user account needed. **Pattern:** when testing client-side permission gating, this is faster than provisioning a dedicated low-privilege test user and avoids invite-email flows. Restore is non-negotiable; do it in the same turn.

- **Latent bugs hide in untaken paths — and a literal RPC carry-forward preserves the schema assumptions, not just the body.** Surfaced during 67c1 T23 Test 12. The 67b cleanup migration added `code` to `estimate_line_items` and the `convert_estimate_to_invoice` RPC has been INSERTing into `invoice_line_items (..., code, ...)` since 67b cleanup landed. But neither 67b foundation nor cleanup ever ALTER'd `invoice_line_items` to add the column. The bug was latent for ~4 days because no real conversion ran in prod (0 invoices with line items). T20's QB sync swap from `xactimate_code` → `code` referenced the same missing column but never executed against an invoice with line items either. T21's literal carry-forward of the live RPC body preserved the broken INSERT. Fix at `dd66b2f`. **Pattern:** when a build's primary code path has zero real-world traffic in prod (post-foundation feature flag, freshly added flow, etc.), file a manual end-to-end check as a chip — don't rely on tsc + `npm run build` to surface column-existence issues. Transactional DO-block testing on real data (with `RAISE EXCEPTION` rollback) is the canonical mechanism for these flows; T23 Test 12's DO-block was what surfaced this.

- **Permissions admin-bypass at `permissions-api.ts:44` is by design but counter-intuitive when testing.** `if (membership.role === "admin") return ok: true` short-circuits before the permission check. To get a 403 from a manage-permission gate, you must demote `user_organizations.role` to `crew_lead` AND revoke the permission. Toggling the permission row alone does nothing for admins. Surfaced during 67c1 T23 Test 11.

- **`useState(prop)` initializes once — server-driven prop advances need an explicit re-sync.** Surfaced during 67b Task 52 (Test 2 apply-template UI didn't update after success toast). Builder root pattern was `const [state, setState] = useState({ entity })` — when parent server-component re-fetched after `router.refresh()` and re-rendered with a new `entity` prop, the child's local state ignored it. Fix at `a936be0`: add `useEffect` keyed on a stable identifier (`[entity.data.id, entity.data.updated_at]`) that calls `setState({ entity })`. Need `eslint-disable-next-line react-hooks/exhaustive-deps` because the linter wants the entire `entity` object in deps, but that would clobber every parent re-render and overwrite optimistic auto-save state. **Pattern:** anywhere local component state mirrors a server-fetched prop — especially in builder/editor shells where the server component re-fetches after a mutation — needs a re-sync effect keyed on identity + version. Worth a sweep across other client components that take a server-rendered entity prop.

- **5-minute pre-flight on plan code blocks before dispatching a milestone batch saves dispatch rework.** Caught 5 plan-codebase divergences before kicking off Tasks 34–52 in 67b session 9: (1) Tasks 40 + 43 assumed a builder root prop API (`<EstimateBuilder mode=...>`) that didn't exist; (2) Task 34 imported from `@/components/ui/combobox` which didn't exist; (3) Task 36 missing `router.refresh()` after apply-template; (4) Task 41 assumed nested settings-nav groups when codebase has flat one; (5) Task 42 needed `getActiveOrganizationId` 400 guard. Each would have caused a fix iteration during dispatch. Collapsed into a Task 33.5 + plan inline-edit pass before any subagent ran. **Pattern:** before dispatching a new milestone batch, grep the named imports + verify the call signatures + scan for `router.refresh()` / orgId guards / settings-nav patterns against the actual codebase. Especially relevant for plans drafted weeks ago against an evolving codebase.

- **For builder-shell prop type widening across modes, use a discriminated union over the props object — not a single broadened `entity` prop.** Task 28's HeaderBar refactor: prop type went from `{ estimate: Estimate; ... }` to `{ mode: "estimate"; entity: Estimate; ...common } | { mode: "invoice"; entity: Invoice; ...common } | { mode: "template"; entity: TemplateWithContents; ...common }`. This lets tsc narrow `entity` cleanly inside each mode-branch without casts (`entity.status` resolves to the entity-specific status enum). A single broadened `entity: Estimate | Invoice | TemplateWithContents` prop with `mode` as a separate discriminator does NOT auto-narrow without an explicit type predicate or `if (mode === "X") { const e = entity as X; ... }` cast. **Pattern to remember:** when threading a discriminator and a polymorphic value through a component, lift them into the union at the props level so tsc's narrowing is automatic. Also useful when this same pattern lands on Task 41/42's template builder host and Task 47's read-only invoice view.

- **Plan code blocks lie about which files fetch in this codebase.** Task 32 plan listed 4 files (section-card, subsection-card, line-item-row, add-item-dialog) needing entityBase URL rewriting. In actuality: only add-item-dialog.tsx makes its own fetches; the 3 layout components are pure presentational and delegate every mutation through parent callbacks. Caught by a 30-second `grep -nE "fetch\(.*api/estimates"` before dispatching. **Pattern:** for any plan task that lists multiple files with the words "all", "each", or "every", grep first; the plan was drafted against a hypothetical codebase shape that may not match. Especially relevant for Tasks 41/42 (template editor host) and 47 (invoice read-only rewrite) where the plan likely assumes patterns from earlier prototypes.

- **Type aliases preserve names but not shapes.** During 67b Task 10, the initial commit aliased `InvoiceWithContents as InvoiceWithItems` thinking the rename would suffice for the kept callers — but the new type has nested `sections[]` and the old type had flat `line_items[]`. Six callers broke at tsc (PDF route writes `invoice.line_items = items`, PDF doc reads `invoice.line_items.map`, etc.). Fix at `9eae494`: standalone deprecated `InvoiceWithItems` interface holding the original flat shape, scoped to legacy callers being replaced in Tasks 14/15/47. **Pattern:** when migrating a type, grep for the old type name's *field accesses* (`.line_items.map`, etc.), not just imports. Names lie about shapes. The C2-strategy interview with the user (Option 1 / 2 / 3 trade-off) plus structured JSDoc + verification grep command is the canonical way to handle this.

- **Plan code blocks drift from actual codebase signatures.** The 67b plan's spec'd `requirePermission` calling convention (`if (denied) return denied;`) doesn't tsc — the actual function returns a discriminated union (`{ ok: true; userId } | { ok: false; response }`). Same with `getActiveOrganizationId` returning `string | null` despite plan code passing it directly into a strict-string param. Surfaced in 67b Task 14, applied uniformly going forward. **Pattern:** before trusting a plan code block's import + call, read the actual exported signature from the lib. A 5-minute pre-flight against `permissions-api.ts`, `get-active-org.ts`, `api-errors.ts`, `postgrest.ts` would have caught both before any subagent dispatched. Worth doing once at plan-review time rather than ten times during execution.

- **Subagent harness can't always reach prod Supabase.** Live browser verification via the Claude Preview MCP fails inside subagent dispatch (`ENOTFOUND` on the project's Supabase hostname). For tasks that require browser verification, defer to local-environment runs or fold into the build's final manual test pass. Surfaced during 67b Task 7's `use-auto-save.ts` refactor verification — filed as V1 cleanup chip for §11 final test coverage.

- **build52 lesson** — GoTrue panics on NULL token columns in `auth.users`. Use empty strings instead, never NULL. See [[2026-04-22-build52-null-tokens-lesson]].
- **Build 66 numbering collision** — "Build 66" labels two unrelated threads: (1) [[build-66]], the soft-delete jobs feature (PR #37, migration build66, shipped); and (2) [[build-66a]] / [[build-66b]] / [[build-66c]] / [[build-66d]], the Knowledge Vault meta-spec. Different scopes, same prefix because the migration counter and the meta-spec independently chose 66.
- **Jarvis migrations are 21, 23, 25a, 26b** — earlier briefings said "21, 25a, 27, 28" but 27 and 28 are email features (categories, body-patterns), not Jarvis. The actual Jarvis-ecosystem migrations are 21 (Jarvis Core), 23 (R&D), 25a (Knowledge + Field Ops), 26b (Marketing). Source: file-name reading + content checks during 66b audit.
- **Build IDs vs migration numbers diverge after Build 14.** See [[00-glossary]].
- **`.gitignore` directory exclude blocks child negation.** `.claude/` (directory pattern) cannot be re-included via `!.claude/skills/` — git can't re-include files inside an excluded parent. Use `.claude/*` (wildcard children) so each entry is evaluated against the negation list. Git docs (`gitignore(5)`): "It is not possible to re-include a file if a parent directory of that file is excluded." Same fix pattern as `.yarn/*` (lines 7–11) and `/out/*` (lines 18–20). Surfaced during [[build-66c]] when the new `.claude/skills/` files weren't trackable despite the negation lines.
- **`preview_start` ignores `launch.json` `runtimeExecutable`/`runtimeArgs`.** The Claude Preview MCP's `preview_start` always runs `npm run dev` regardless of the launch.json config name, which on TheLaunchPad loads the parent worktree's prod `.env.local` under Next.js's workspace-root inference (it detects `C:\Users\14252\package-lock.json` as the workspace root and pulls env files from there). The first scratch smoke test during [[2026-04-29-build-65b]] connected to **prod** Supabase before this was caught — the failed login was a 400 (no actual prod data modified) but the next attempt with a real password would have. Workaround: invoke the dev server directly via Bash with `npx dotenv -e .env.scratch.local -- npm run dev -- --port 3001`. Documented in `supabase/scratch-replay-notes.md`.
- **`invoice_line_items` already had `sort_order` + `xactimate_code` from Build 38.** During the [[build-67a]] migration, the v1.0 ALTER block tried to add both again and the migration failed transactionally before any other change landed. The retry only adds `section_id`, `library_item_id`, `unit`. Surface `xactimate_code` as `code` and `amount` as `total` in TS via mapper at the API-route boundary (same pattern as `invoices.total_amount` ↔ `Invoice.total`). **General lesson:** before writing an ALTER ADD against a multi-build-touched table, run `\d <table>` in SQL or query `information_schema.columns` — every prior build's ALTER is invisible from the newest migration file.

- **PostgREST `.is(col, value)` only accepts `null`/`true`/`false`/`unknown` — passing a UUID silently fails at runtime.** Surfaced during [[build-67a]] Task 9 code review (commit `0aae288`); fixed at `4e53cc3` by branching the query: `.eq` for the UUID case, `.is(_, null)` for the null case. The TS type system signs off because `supabase-js` types `.is()`'s second arg loosely. Any future query that does `.is("col", value_that_might_be_a_uuid_or_null)` against a nullable foreign-key column has the same bug. The canonical pattern is: `if (uuid) q = q.eq(col, uuid); else q = q.is(col, null);`. Plan part-2 calls this out in the "Hardening notes" section.

- **Plan ↔ codebase divergence on settings page architecture.** Plan part-2's UI tasks were drafted assuming patterns that don't exist in this repo: `settings-nav.ts` has no group infrastructure / no permission filtering (Task 15 plan said "Catalog collapsible group with permission visibility"); `src/lib/permissions.ts` doesn't exist and every settings CRUD page is a single client component using `useAuth().hasPermission()` (Task 18 plan said "server component + client split"). Both were collapsed to match the existing pattern (Eric chose Option A for Task 15 explicitly; controller adjusted Task 18 with announcement). **Pre-flight the references named in plan part-2 against the actual codebase before locking SDD prompts for Tasks 19–30.** Especially: confirm `src/components/form-builder/canvas.tsx` has the dnd-kit exports the builder UI tasks expect, and `src/components/tiptap-editor.tsx` has the Tiptap wrapper the statement editors expect.

- **`form_config` had a long-standing latent bug from build46.** Migration build46 added a unique index `form_config_org_key` on `(organization_id)` alone — collapsing each tenant to a single row. The unchanged `/api/settings/intake-form` POST route did `INSERT` with `version+1`, so every save after the first per-org silently 500'd with a duplicate-key violation. Eric had been editing AAA's form for months without noticing — the toast read "Save failed" and was assumed transient. Surfaced during [[build-14j]] verification when the new always-visible version pill made the failure mode loud. Fix: [[build-14j]] Task 0 migration replaced the singleton with a composite `(organization_id, version)` unique. **Worth scanning other settings pages for the same shape** — any POST route that does `INSERT` with `version+1` against a table whose unique index is `(organization_id)` instead of `(organization_id, version)` will have the same issue.

- **PostgREST `.contains(col, jsArray)` against a `jsonb` column emits invalid Postgres syntax.** supabase-js's `.contains()` serializes a JS array as a Postgres array literal `{x,y}`. That works against `text[]` columns but fails against `jsonb` columns with `"invalid input syntax for type json"` because PostgREST's `cs` operator on jsonb requires the value to be JSON-formatted (`["x","y"]`). Surfaced during [[build-67a]] post-ship browser verification — `damage_type_tags` and `section_tags` are `jsonb NOT NULL DEFAULT '[]'::jsonb` (per migration-build67a, lines 24-25), and AddItemDialog's library tab toasted the error when Eric clicked into the dialog with a damage_type chip pre-applied. Fix at `3bc2617`: pass JSON-stringified value — `.contains("damage_type_tags", JSON.stringify([value]))`. **Canonical pattern:** if the column is jsonb (check the migration), wrap the array in `JSON.stringify()`; if text[], pass the JS array directly. **Worth a sweep across the codebase** — `grep -r "\.contains(" src/` to find other callers and verify each against its column type.

- **Auto-save fetches need explicit timeouts.** A hung connection (mobile network drop, slow server) without `AbortController` makes React's saveStatus stick in `"saving"` forever; `inFlightRef` stays `true`, blocking subsequent debounced saves. The estimate builder's `useAutoSave` hook hit this in code review (commit `cb26a0b` fix) — added `FETCH_TIMEOUT_MS = 30_000` + `AbortController` to all four save paths (estimate-level PUT, line-item PUT, sections-reorder PUT, line-items-reorder PUT). AbortError is routed to the same error path as network errors. **General lesson:** any client-side fetch that sets a "saving" status flag needs a timeout-and-abort cycle; otherwise the flag is a lie under network failure.

- **Snapshot-based concurrency guards must bump the parent's `updated_at` even on no-op-looking child mutations.** The 67a I2 fix (commit `4a85c7e`) added server-side `updated_at_snapshot` enforcement to the sections + line-items reorder PUTs. Reorders only touch child rows (`estimate_sections.sort_order`, `estimate_line_items.sort_order` / `section_id`); the parent `estimates` row would otherwise stay quiet, so two concurrent reorders against the same snapshot would both succeed and the second would silently overwrite the first's order. Fix: every mutation route that the snapshot guard protects must also `touchEstimate(supabase, estimateId)` (no-op `UPDATE estimates SET updated_at = now()` — the BEFORE-UPDATE trigger handles the actual value) so the next snapshot read sees the change. New helpers in `lib/estimates.ts`: `checkSnapshot` + `touchEstimate`. **General lesson:** if a route is guarded by `updated_at_snapshot` against a parent table but only writes to a child table, you must explicitly bump the parent's `updated_at` after the child write or the guard is a lie under concurrency.

- **PostgREST `.or()` accepts user input as comma-separated filter syntax — escape it.** The 67a Phase C sweep fixed three callers (`lib/item-library.ts`, `components/job-detail.tsx`, `api/email/contacts/route.ts`) where user-typed input was concatenated into an `.or(...)` filter expression. A search like `foo,bar` would be parsed as two filters with `bar` as a column-name fragment, which fails the request; worse, a value like `,deleted=is.true` could in principle escape into additional conditions (RLS contains the blast radius but the bug is real). Fix: new `lib/postgrest.ts` → `escapeOrFilterValue` wraps the value in PostgREST's documented quoted form (`"value"`) and escapes embedded `\` / `"`. `%` and `_` stay as ilike wildcards by design. **Canonical pattern:** any `.or(...)` or `.and(...)` whose value contains user input goes through the helper.

- **API routes should never return raw `error.message` on 5xx.** Postgres / Supabase errors leak schema details, constraint names, RLS policy text, and sometimes the offending row contents. Phase C added `lib/api-errors.ts` (`apiError` + `apiDbError`) that logs the full message server-side and returns `{error: "internal error"}` to the client. Wired into all 67a + item-library routes; the remaining ~80 routes still leak and are filed as a follow-up sweep. **Canonical pattern:** at every 5xx site, replace `NextResponse.json({ error: error.message }, { status: 500 })` with `apiDbError(error.message, "<METHOD> <route> <op>")`.

- **2026-05-09** — Build 65c upload pipeline shipped + smoke-verified end-to-end on Eric's iPhone via local Xcode install (151 photos uploaded to AAA prod `photos` table for the test job with full metadata: 1080×1920 dimensions, file_size, taken_by, uploaded_from='mobile'); PR #52 open against `main` with Vercel preview green. Two bugs surfaced + fixed (commit `3cf8d04`): **Bug A** — `UploadQueueWorker` only scanned disk on provider mount so live captures were invisible until next launch; fix dispatches a `'65c-capture-written'` window event from `writeCapture` that triggers worker rescan + drain. **Bug B** — `CameraView.stopCamera`'s `if (!startedRef.current) return` guard left the native camera running when the user exited between mount and `CameraPreview.start()` resolving (visible: live camera leak through iOS status-bar safe-area on next page); fix drops the guard. **Topology gotcha worth remembering**: `capacitor.config.ts`'s `server.url` pins the iOS WebView to prod, so PR-preview smoke testing needs a temp config override pointing at the PR's Vercel preview URL (don't commit). **Next.js routing gotcha**: app-router excludes `_`-prefixed directories from routing, so the test endpoint `src/app/api/_test/photo-upload-fail/` was silently dropped from the build until renamed to `api/test/...`. **WebView console gotcha**: `await import("@capacitor/<plugin>")` throws "Module name does not resolve to a valid URL" in Safari Web Inspector against the iPhone — use `window.Capacitor.Plugins.<Plugin>` for ad-hoc diagnostics. **UX surprise to validate next**: after Bug A fix, captures upload + delete from local disk during the shutter session, so the Review screen shows "0 photos" if everything uploaded — pipeline is correct but the empty-state message is misleading; filed for 65b.1.
